  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8ae286dc-034b-413f-b1ab-288a10c965b5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="review_1366145776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1366145776" />
    <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf"><img alt="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540171256p2/9185509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1366145776?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf">Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442350083" href="/book/show/13545314-gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1366145776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6491266869475062544">This is my first Tess Gerritsen book. I know right? I'm a crime and thriller fan, AND a nurse... I should have read all the Rizzole and Isles by now!?? Well I never intended to, but having read this one I am inclined to give all of her books a go!<br/><br/>To quickly summarise it, some bizarre virus is killing off the crew of the international space station. Where did it come from?? How are they going to stop it? Doctor on board Emma must try to keep everyone alive whilst her husband back on earth goes on</span>
  <span id="freeText6491266869475062544" style="display:none">This is my first Tess Gerritsen book. I know right? I'm a crime and thriller fan, AND a nurse... I should have read all the Rizzole and Isles by now!?? Well I never intended to, but having read this one I am inclined to give all of her books a go!<br /><br />To quickly summarise it, some bizarre virus is killing off the crew of the international space station. Where did it come from?? How are they going to stop it? Doctor on board Emma must try to keep everyone alive whilst her husband back on earth goes on a mission to discover the origins of the pathogen.<br /><br />Great read! Extremely suspenseful and exciting! Loved the whole thing! Yes, it was pretty corny... But it was supposed to be! I thought it was fantastic!<br /><br />The characters were great! Soon to be ex husband and wife Emma and Jack are a great team.<br /><br />The audio version was fantastic. The narrator was wonderfully talented and probably the best narrator of any audio book I have listened to so far. Even his portrayal of the female characters was fantastic and he really captured the emotion of all the characters.<br /><br />There was quite a bit of blood and gore in this book and I really enjoyed it! Because most of the gory scenes happen in space it added an extra grossness... Floating blood etc. Thought it was really well done.<br /><br />Some of the medical scenes were totally over the top, but Dr Gerritsen obviously knows her stuff as everything was quite accurate. I guess that is what makes her one of the top medical thriller authors.<br /><br />Would I recommend it?<br /><br />Yes it was great fun! Really enjoyed it. Any thriller and fan of a little space blood and guts will love Gravity! I've already started putting her other books on my TBR list!<br /><br />For more reviews, visit my blog<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.booksbabiesbeing.com">www.booksbabiesbeing.com</a><br />Follow me on twitter<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/BBB_Mel">www.twitter.com/BBB_Mel</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6491266869475062544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1137748048291115997" style="display:none">Wow! This was SO good. I can't think why I have never read it before. And why oh why did I not go and see the movie.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694322293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11209212981484818668">Before reading this, I had few expectations. Just knowing that the author writes popular police procedurals doesn't always mean that other genres are a cinch to write. So I had to back off and just let the tale tell itself.<br/><br/>I let myself flow into the story as it began heavily on the characterization and it slowly turned into a medical thriller just happening to take place in space. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670.The_Andromeda_Strain' title='The Andromeda Strain by Michael Crichton' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Andromeda Strain</a>?   <span id="freeText11209212981484818668" style="display:none">Before reading this, I had few expectations. Just knowing that the author writes popular police procedurals doesn't always mean that other genres are a cinch to write. So I had to back off and just let the tale tell itself.<br /><br />I let myself flow into the story as it began heavily on the characterization and it slowly turned into a medical thriller just happening to take place in space. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670.The_Andromeda_Strain" title="The Andromeda Strain by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Andromeda Strain</a>? Hmmm. But then the modern storytelling style got me hooked. No one behaved unreasonably. Smart, strong characters. Rising tension... and then somewhere in the middle, I found myself thrilling to the horror of it. :)<br /><br />There's plenty of cool biology and medical thriller stuff, but you know what I found most interesting? It had cool echoes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/66479.Starfish__Rifters___1_" title="Starfish (Rifters, #1) by Peter Watts" rel="nofollow noopener">Starfish</a>. It even reminded me a bit of that movie, Life. Or conjure in your mind any rampant story of contagion, and you've got a great idea about where this novel is headed.<br /><br />I have very few complaints. I had a great time throughout. But if I should feel the need to complain about anything... it's the end. I'm not sure I buy it.<br /><br />But other than that, I think I had a lot more fun here than I thought I would. :) Tess really can write SF thrillers. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11209212981484818668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155089141?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007888450" href="/book/show/25887597-gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155089141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9719639636648455780">As Doctor Emma Watson exited the simulator training module after yet another simulated mission, she knew she was ready. The whole team would be ready to head into space when scheduled in three months’ time. But the unexpected emergency involving one of the current astronauts at the space station meant he needed to be brought home – and Emma was chosen as his replacement. Emma was a research physician, excellent at her job; her estranged and soon to be divorced husband Doctor Jack McCallum was al</span>
  <span id="freeText9719639636648455780" style="display:none">As Doctor Emma Watson exited the simulator training module after yet another simulated mission, she knew she was ready. The whole team would be ready to head into space when scheduled in three months’ time. But the unexpected emergency involving one of the current astronauts at the space station meant he needed to be brought home – and Emma was chosen as his replacement. Emma was a research physician, excellent at her job; her estranged and soon to be divorced husband Doctor Jack McCallum was also involved with the space program, but a medical condition meant he was unable to go into orbit – Jack used his surgical and specialist abilities at a civilian hospital while watching from afar.<br /><br />Once Emma had settled into life aboard the space station, the intrigue and fascination of space once again held her in its grip. But when one of their crew members became ill, Emma struggled to diagnose his problem. She knew he needed to be evacuated immediately – but as the horror of what was happening intensified, the crew on the space station plus their support from NASA knew they were up against something catastrophic – the danger was not just to the astronauts but to anyone who came into contact with them. What would happen to Emma and the courageous crew? What could Jack and NASA do in their fight to bring them home?<br /><br />Wow! <i>Gravity</i> by Tess Gerritsen is unbelievably tense and gripping! It is a psychological thriller by an author who knows her craft and knows how to entertain her readers. I flew through the 500 pages of this book with my heart racing - it has an excellent plot which reads easily. Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9719639636648455780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2636058102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2636058102" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2636058102?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442350083" href="/book/show/13545314-gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2636058102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9817440773912568815">Turns out, I have known this author's work for a while. Because my sister is a fan of the TV show <i>Rizzoli & Isles</i> which is based on a book series by this author. Nevertheless, this was my first book by her.<br/><br/>We follow Emma Watson and a few other astronauts as they are getting ready to go on a mission to the ISS. While on board, some experiment goes horribly wrong because suddenly people are infected with <i>something</i> and the race to find out what it is begins.<br/>Naturally, back down on Earth, people are</span>
  <span id="freeText9817440773912568815" style="display:none">Turns out, I have known this author's work for a while. Because my sister is a fan of the TV show <i>Rizzoli &amp; Isles</i> which is based on a book series by this author. Nevertheless, this was my first book by her.<br><br>We follow Emma Watson and a few other astronauts as they are getting ready to go on a mission to the ISS. While on board, some experiment goes horribly wrong because suddenly people are infected with <i>something</i> and the race to find out what it is begins.<br>Naturally, back down on Earth, people are trying to help but depending on what <i>it</i> is, it's too dangerous to allow the crew back home.<br><br>There is a little politicking but mostly it's science. The science of getting people into space (physics) as much as chemistry and biology. And wonderful bodily horror once people start dying. Think <i>Contagion</i> but on a station in Earth's orbit. <br>Naturally, it helps that the author knows her facts (she's a doctor in anthropology and medicine) and she has a wonderful way of filling this book to the brim with those facts but in such a neat way that they seamlessly blend with the suspense of having to solve the mystery of what is going on, how it is possible and if it can be stopped.<br><br>However, as much as I liked getting to know the NASA staff, the flight crews, and following the experiments as well as the inter-personal relationships on the ISS, the ending was almost a bit of a letdown. I mean, not only <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[did Emma survive (thanks to her hero husband) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but she also <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[woke up and recovered despite having been on Death's threshold ... think about it, the cure was just fighting the chimera, that thing had already done considerable damage to her body <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Moreover, the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the chimera still exists on Earth, down in the ocean near the Galápagos islands, waiting in that submerged asteroid ... there is a strong current around there so it could simply be swept to places and infect people but the government isn't taking precautions <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>?! That was all ... I don't know. I think what troubled me the most was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[what kind of "miracle" was found - the cure lying in pregnancy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. However, the author IS a medical doctor so she would know if that was at least partially realistic and I did like the thought of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[an alien species being out there and unleashing this chimera like seeds on the wind to colonize other planets <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548972935i/26997677._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Don't let that smile fool you, this lady is a killer!)<br><br>All in all, the above mentioned points are relatively minor complaints, just thoughts floating around my head while reading the book and now that I've finished it and I'd love to have a chance to talk to the author about her thought process. <br><br>Anyway, the action was relentless, the characters were extremely lively (making you suffer with them), and the science was superb (I cannot say if that one thing bugging me would be scientifically accurate) so the book still gets full marks for being so different from other thrillers and engaging and for it demanding a smart reader. Besides, who doesn't like an experiment gone wrong - in space! - that has the potential of either wiping out humanity or at the very least decimating us like the zombie apocalypse?!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9817440773912568815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13343059-gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer13463855802314251805"><br/>Tess Gerritsen moves the setting for her medical thriller to space and boy is it scary! Emma Watson is a doctor and astronaut who is thrilled to finally be able to go into space and work in the space station. However, when a strange illness begins to affect the crew, she finds herself struggling to work out what is wrong with them. Back on Earth her husband Jack can only watch while her colleagues at NASA try to work out how to save the crew.<br/><br/>An excellent page turner of a sci fi thriller! </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1956144933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1956144933" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604273386p2/64621419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1956144933?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671016777" href="/book/show/903442.Gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1956144933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12018845765484204602">“For the past thirty years, Michael Crichton’s <i>The Andromeda Strain</i> has served as the benchmark … not anymore. Tess Gerritsen sets the new standard with <i>Gravity</i> … one of those rare books that scares you for all the right reasons.“ <br/><blockquote>-The Providence Sunday Journal</blockquote><br/><br/>I’m a fan of Crichton’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670.The_Andromeda_Strain__Andromeda___1_' title='The Andromeda Strain (Andromeda, #1) by Michael Crichton' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Andromeda Strain</a>. So in my ears that’s pretty high praise. And the book didn’t disappoint.<br/><br/>Dr. Emma Watson is sent to the International Space Station after the wife of the physician aboard ISS had a terrible car</span>
  <span id="freeText12018845765484204602" style="display:none">“For the past thirty years, Michael Crichton’s <i>The Andromeda Strain</i> has served as the benchmark … not anymore. Tess Gerritsen sets the new standard with <i>Gravity</i> … one of those rare books that scares you for all the right reasons.“ <br><blockquote>-The Providence Sunday Journal</blockquote><br><br>I’m a fan of Crichton’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670.The_Andromeda_Strain__Andromeda___1_" title="The Andromeda Strain (Andromeda, #1) by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Andromeda Strain</a>. So in my ears that’s pretty high praise. And the book didn’t disappoint.<br><br>Dr. Emma Watson is sent to the International Space Station after the wife of the physician aboard ISS had a terrible car accident and NASA decides to bring him back home.<br>Watson had been very eager to go to space and even though the circumstances are unfortunate she’s relishing the opportunity.<br><br>But on ISS an experiment with some mice goes wrong and one of the astronauts gets seriously ill. Watson, as the physician on duty, is tending to the patient who’s vital signs start to show some peculiar developments. She can’t quite figure out what’s going on. And neither can NASA.<br><br>Soon things start to go horribly wrong and the situation threatens to get completely out of hand. With the disease spreading amongst the astronauts.<br><br>In the beginning my fascination with the Space Program flared up once again and I was in awe of the things human beings are able to achieve.<br><br>But we are also capable of fucking up big time and space is not exactly the best place to make mistakes. Not even small ones.<br><br>Very quickly this became a highly suspenseful medical thriller, where the reader is trying to figure out what exactly went wrong. And a lot of things do go wrong and Dr. Watson is always at a disadvantage because of her challenging surroundings.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545580087ra/26796537.gif" width="400" height="227" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As things go from bad to worse, the military is butting in and it becomes clear that we are dealing with something significant.<br><br>Until the point when it is finally revealed what’s causing the disease, this indeed felt very much like <i>The Andromeda Strain</i> in space. And an all-around better version of it even, because while there is a ton of science in Gerritsen‘s book as well, it offers a better realised plot and slightly more interesting characters.<br><br>When it’s finally clear what happened and attempts to rescue the astronauts and cure the disease became the major plot points, it wasn’t quite as good as before. But still highly entertaining.<br><br>In addition to <i>The Andromeda Strain</i> I also got some vibes of <i>Alien</i>, <i>The Martian</i> and the Wolfgang Petersen movie <i>Outbreak</i>.<br>It's great fun!<br><br>This book goes right onto my favorites shelf. And I’ll be looking for more works from the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12018845765484204602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9231500003547405251">About 15 years ago I read the first Rizzoli & Isles thriller, The Surgeon, and liked it. And although I 5-starred it, I never again picked up anything by Gerritsen. Well, space and an infection sounded too tempting to pass up. And after finishing this book, I think I should have picked up something by Gerritsen sooner.<br/><br/>On the book it mentions ER meets Apollo 13. Throw in Andromeda Strain by Michael Crichton and we have a deal. And maybe bits of Life and Contagion.<br/><br/>Gordon Obie, known as the Sphinx.</span>
  <span id="freeText9231500003547405251" style="display:none">About 15 years ago I read the first Rizzoli &amp; Isles thriller, The Surgeon, and liked it. And although I 5-starred it, I never again picked up anything by Gerritsen. Well, space and an infection sounded too tempting to pass up. And after finishing this book, I think I should have picked up something by Gerritsen sooner.<br /><br />On the book it mentions ER meets Apollo 13. Throw in Andromeda Strain by Michael Crichton and we have a deal. And maybe bits of Life and Contagion.<br /><br />Gordon Obie, known as the Sphinx... that got old eventually. I am also not a massive fan of the whole conspiracy theory shindig and the mysterious grey haired billionaire. And the ending seemed a bit too easy.<br /><br />Setting that aside, this was a very enjoyable read, full of action and suspense and plenty of gross bodily fluids. Whilst I started slowly, I read the bulk of the book in one day and had a hard time putting it down. Well done!</span>

<div id="review_1863315763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1863315763" />
    <a title="Paula Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60858230-paula-brandon"><img alt="Paula Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477272707p2/60858230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1863315763?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula Brandon" href="/user/show/60858230-paula-brandon">Paula Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1863315763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8529861307099718268">Wow, what a great thriller! Tess Gerritsen has always been one of my favourite authors, but I stayed away from this one because of the whole lawsuit over the movie thing. All of a sudden, Gerritsen seemed to be accusing any movie set at the International Space Station of ripping off her book, and wasn't afraid to say so on social media. Then she was complaining about readers not understanding the ending to "Playing With Fire"....and well, I was a little put off, both by Gerritsen as an author an</span>
  <span id="freeText8529861307099718268" style="display:none">Wow, what a great thriller! Tess Gerritsen has always been one of my favourite authors, but I stayed away from this one because of the whole lawsuit over the movie thing. All of a sudden, Gerritsen seemed to be accusing any movie set at the International Space Station of ripping off her book, and wasn't afraid to say so on social media. Then she was complaining about readers not understanding the ending to "Playing With Fire"....and well, I was a little put off, both by Gerritsen as an author and tackling "Gravity" the book.<br /><br />However, a bit of time has passed since then, and I'm glad I gave this a try, because it was a fast-paced thrill ride. Although this book is to do with a mission into space and obviously meticulously researched, it was never overwhelmed with too much research on the page and endless technical jargon. Believe me, mine are the first eyes to glaze over if there is too much of that - and has even done so in other Gerritsen books - but that was never the case here. It maintained a feverish pace from start to finish.<br /><br />Heroine Emma Watson, a doctor, is added to a space crew at the ISS after a family tragedy sees an existing member exit. She joins right around the time one of their experiments is contaminated and infects one of the crew members. Attempts to get this crew member evacuated sees events spiraling out of control. The hero is Emma's soon-to-be ex-husband, Jack McCallum, who had to exit the astronaut program due to health risks. His love for Emma is reignited by his efforts to help bring her and the other astronauts home.<br /><br />"Gravity" is an exciting space thriller with lots of gooey action and gore as the bacteria/lifeform infects various astronauts one by one with messy results. I read it in one go. This book bears very little similarity to the movie "Gravity", so ignore all that business with the lawsuit. This is very much a sci-fi/medical/horror thriller as opposed to the straight-out survival theme of the movie. It was a tale I literally couldn't put down, and pretty much read in one go! <br /><br />There are some quibbles that keep this from 4 stars. Firstly, there are too many characters. I started writing down the names of them all so that I could keep track. Nearly every chapter seemed to introduce a new one. It could get a little confusing, so I needed my own personal cheat sheet to keep up! Secondly, it needed more focus on Emma and the other astronauts, stranded in space and dying under gruesome circumstances. They were the characters we needed to know the most about and care about, because they were the ones in peril. Too much time was spent on the ground with Jack, and various meetings the government/military/NASA undertook to determine what they felt the fate of the astronauts should be. Too often, I was thinking, "Get back to the space station!" That's where the action was, and it was frustrating to be pulled back to Earth so often for another meeting.<br /><br />But otherwise, this kept me hooked from start to finish. I'd love to see this properly adapted as a movie or TV series, it's that exciting! Sadly, after battling Hollywood over the movie "Gravity" and what she sees as plagiarism by other films, as well as the end of the "Rizzoli &amp; Isles" TV series, Tess Gerritsen seems to have given up writing books, and moved to script-writing. Guess I'll be tuning into her films, then! But definitely give this one a look.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8529861307099718268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText451755770607281308" style="display:none">To give you an idea of how good this book was, I’m seriously considering changing almost all of my 5 star book reviews to 4 stars because they don’t meet the standards this novel has given me. <br /><br />I swear to God when I signed up to read a book for English, I didn’t want to go on this emotional roller coaster the book brought me on. <br /><br />The characters are lovable, but they all have their own flaws. It's better than a Michael Crichton book in my opinion. If you're easily "grossed out", though, you might think twice before starting it, but it's worth whatever it takes to read! </span>

  <span id="freeText16607490364895059041" style="display:none">Tess Gerritsens book Gravity is one of those books that could make millions at the movies if someone would just make it . This book has everything Science ,Space,medicine and horrible death.<br />When Dr Emma Watson starts her duty on the international space station she find a horror thats beyond imagination . Some how a single celled organism has found it way on board and has regenerated out of control .<br />People on the station are dieing in horrible ways and Emma could be next if she cant find a solution . NASA is at a loss as to how to help her as Emma's estranged husband Jack McCallum tires desperately to bring her home safely . Word of the horrible infection has caused the government to stop anyone from coming home and they are all running out of time to save the station as the astronauts start dieing from the contagion . With little help from home and the wrong equipment to help her Emma must find a cure, but how and How could this even happen . the answers will amaze you . Warning this is not for the easily grossed out lol the deaths are very graphic and resemble Ebola or a Ebola like disease but in a zero gravity environment .</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16104096940074369377">Ok where to start - I really did enjoy this book and even though it took its time getting up to speed (and I will admit there were times when I was wondering where certain scenes in the story were going to have any relevance) but I must admit once it was up to speed it was a real page turner.   <span id="freeText16104096940074369377" style="display:none">Ok where to start - I really did enjoy this book and even though it took its time getting up to speed (and I will admit there were times when I was wondering where certain scenes in the story were going to have any relevance) but I must admit once it was up to speed it was a real page turner. I will say that I feel that after reading this I should read more of her work but at the same time I feel that considering the authors popularity and the number of books written that I may need to do a lot more research to be truly able to pass comment on how good this book is. I will admit that the some aspects seemed very convenient and others picked up from other story lines but that to me didn't matter - I loved how the various pieces slowly came together and resolved themselves but at the same time didn't give you that chocolate box finish that makes it feel a little "too" perfect/ <br />One this I will throw in here too - is that reading this all the comments about the space shuttles doe age the book but in a good way - it makes me nostalgic for those amazing craft and long for the day something equally awe inspiring takes to the skies </span>
  <a data-text-id="16104096940074369377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2292203323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14777373599322497262">First off, no, this has nothing to do with the movie of the same name. Both have female astronauts as a main character, but that's about it. Second, one of the main characters is named Emma Watson, but has nothing to do with the famous actress. With that cleared up...<br/><br/>A series of accidents and secrets take a research mission at the International Space Station, and turn it into a nightmare. A strange new disease suddenly breaks out, endangering the entire crew. But it soon becomes apparent that th</span>
  <span id="freeText14777373599322497262" style="display:none">First off, no, this has nothing to do with the movie of the same name. Both have female astronauts as a main character, but that's about it. Second, one of the main characters is named Emma Watson, but has nothing to do with the famous actress. With that cleared up...<br /><br />A series of accidents and secrets take a research mission at the International Space Station, and turn it into a nightmare. A strange new disease suddenly breaks out, endangering the entire crew. But it soon becomes apparent that there's more going on than we knew behind the scenes. The government gets involved, and seem to know a lot more than they are telling. <br /><br />Emma Watson, doctor on the station, is struggling to treat something unlike anything she's ever seen before. Her estranged husband, Jack McCallum, is on the ground, trying to find anything that will help. And there's a struggle going on between NASA and other aspects of the government as, little by little, the secrets behind what's going on come to light. Can the crew be saved? Is Earth in danger from a brand new disease? Will people keep dying to maintain a secret? <br /><br />There's a lot of good drama, tension, and plot twists. I didn't rate it higher because there is some questionable plot devices. One of the people who could have helped stop the chaos dies in random accident just as things kick off. The various contaminations are a bit questionable at times. <br /><br />It's a decent read. Just don't expect the movie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14777373599322497262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_271447841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271447841" />
    <a title="John Jr." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5685608-john-jr"><img alt="John Jr." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311526969p2/5685608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271447841?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Jr." class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Jr." href="/user/show/5685608-john-jr">John Jr.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671016784" href="/book/show/1888063.Gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5685608-john-jr?shelf=medical-thriller">medical-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271447841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6040776845662048206">Medical training in the United States is sometimes put to surprising uses. Tess Gerritsen, like Michael Crichton, earned a medical degree but ended up writing popular fiction with a technical and/or medical angle. One wonders whether the satisfaction (momentary diversion, whatever you want to call it) that both authors have undoubtedly provided to their readers--Gerritsen, while not achieving the household-name status of Crichton, has sold millions of books and reached the NYTBR best-seller list</span>
  <span id="freeText6040776845662048206" style="display:none">Medical training in the United States is sometimes put to surprising uses. Tess Gerritsen, like Michael Crichton, earned a medical degree but ended up writing popular fiction with a technical and/or medical angle. One wonders whether the satisfaction (momentary diversion, whatever you want to call it) that both authors have undoubtedly provided to their readers--Gerritsen, while not achieving the household-name status of Crichton, has sold millions of books and reached the NYTBR best-seller list--is a worthy substitute for the services their medical work might have rendered. Crichton, as <a href="http://www.michaelcrichton.net/aboutmichaelcrichton-biography.html" rel="nofollow noopener">the bio on his website</a> suggests, appears to have done some serious work in research and teaching early on; <a href="http://www.tessgerritsen.com/bio/" rel="nofollow noopener">Gerritsen's bio</a> is less clear about anything beyond her writing. Unless you're willing to equate social value with an author's financial reward, or on the other hand to decide that the presumed nobility of medicine necessarily outweighs entertainment, the question has to be judged a modern-day imponderable. Still, I wonder.<br /><br />Personally, I can't say I'd mind if Gerritsen had never picked up a pen, for that would've saved me the now-vague but still rather potent memories I have of some gruesome details in this book, which were vividly rendered and which are now practically all that remains of the reading experience. Having found a free review copy of <i>Gravity</i> at work one day, I took it home and read it for what I imagine to be a decent reason: simply to find out what was in it. Sometimes one wants a diversion, after all--at least sometimes I do (it's kind of a family tradition)--and this did the trick. Gerritsen handled the requirements of the genre well enough, which is to say that her writing kept me turning the pages while failing in the least to surprise me or to illuminate anything beyond itself. But maybe I should reverse that: while failing to surprise me, etc., the book did keep me reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6040776845662048206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1657369530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1657369530" />
    <a title="Ian Laird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28547777-ian-laird"><img alt="Ian Laird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395488526p2/28547777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1657369530?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Laird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Laird" href="/user/show/28547777-ian-laird">Ian Laird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1657369530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1858290251944138108">Not much like the film, but entertaining in its own right. <br/><br/>Any book which makes you think differently about what you might be doing or how you might see what’s happening around you is worthwhile in my view.<br/><br/>Tess Gerritsen develops the implications of what might happen if scientists start tampering with unknown lifeforms by way of sophisticated genetic engineering.<br/> <br/>This happens when some deep sea scientists find some small critters and after fooling with them put them into space just to see what h</span>
  <span id="freeText1858290251944138108" style="display:none">Not much like the film, but entertaining in its own right. <br /><br />Any book which makes you think differently about what you might be doing or how you might see what’s happening around you is worthwhile in my view.<br /><br />Tess Gerritsen develops the implications of what might happen if scientists start tampering with unknown lifeforms by way of sophisticated genetic engineering.<br /> <br />This happens when some deep sea scientists find some small critters and after fooling with them put them into space just to see what happens.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And what do you know, secretive government agencies are involved up to their eyeballs. The new lifeforms cause all sorts of problems for the mixed crew up in the international space station, mainly by destroying their human hosts, from the inside, sort of boiling them alive and making their appearance in vivid blue and green. Interesting visual image of the globules floating in the zero gravity. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Gerritsen is very good at all the medical details, procedures and all, and she is thorough with her space research. That’s all very authentic. But…characters?<br /><br />Our plucky heroine doctor surgeon astronaut is going through a divorce with her surgeon doctor former astronaut husband. Did I say the heroine (named Emma Watson, just about the time the other (cinematic) Emma Watson made her name as Hermione Granger) is tall, blond and attractive? Of course she is. Anyway many of the people in the story are divorced / going through a divorce. The senior management types are taciturn, but will display true right stuff (there is even a reference to Chuck Yeager) when it counts. Will our plucky heroine get rescued? Will she rescue herself? Will her estranged husband have a kidney stone while hurtling to the rescue?<br /><br />At the end of the day, I was thinking differently about what we do with biohazards and on the lookout for anything vividly blue and green floating through the air, and doing my best to avoid same.<br /><br />Clichéd but rollicking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1858290251944138108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2226998672009241705">Okay. I know I said that I wasn't going to be writing reviews because I just didn't have time. But whoa! I HAD to write something about this mind-bender of a book. I have to say that EVERYTHING about this book was a feast for the brain! When Stephen King said that she was better than Crichton he wasn't kidding. First off, Gerritsen is more readable than Crichton. I find he had a very clinical way of writing that made you disconnect with characters in the book. With this book you are instantly th</span>
  <span id="freeText2226998672009241705" style="display:none">Okay. I know I said that I wasn't going to be writing reviews because I just didn't have time. But whoa! I HAD to write something about this mind-bender of a book. I have to say that EVERYTHING about this book was a feast for the brain! When Stephen King said that she was better than Crichton he wasn't kidding. First off, Gerritsen is more readable than Crichton. I find he had a very clinical way of writing that made you disconnect with characters in the book. With this book you are instantly thrust into POV with the characters and you are connected. Then you have a about a thousand WTF moments before your somehow think you have it all figured out, then your crying because you don't want bad things to happen to these characters you don't particularly like but you don't want them to DIE! Then Gerritsen kicks you right in the rump and you are like OH MY GOD! <br /><br />I know this review is full of gush but it is really hard to write a review on this book, and try to not give it away because you can't give away anything. That is the point of the story, the build, the climb to the top and then the level out which leaves you emotionally drained and ready for her next book. <br /><br />But honestly, I'm so book hung over I don't know what to read next. What is going to top this? I am going to have to read another one of this author's books to appease myself. Never in a million years did I think that a medical suspense novel that takes place in space was going to do it for me as a read. Well, I was just proven wrong. What a fantastic journey I was taken on. And I got to go on the ISS! This book was so well written I felt like I was in space, I even felt dizzy at times with the characters in the book. <br /><br />Highly Recommend! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17518385306535148710">Wow! A friend of mine, both an avid reader and fellow NASA contractor, put this one in my hands. Gravity was published in 1999 so I was late to this party, but it was an amazing read--and I feel safe now in adding that it's timeless. I appreciated Gerritsen's care with technical facts at NASA, as well as her accurate depiction of Johnson Space Center and the Houston area in general. Just a real fun read all-around, close to home for me, and nicely done!<br/><br/>Gerritsen did a remarkable job blurring the</span>
  <span id="freeText17518385306535148710" style="display:none">Wow! A friend of mine, both an avid reader and fellow NASA contractor, put this one in my hands. Gravity was published in 1999 so I was late to this party, but it was an amazing read--and I feel safe now in adding that it's timeless. I appreciated Gerritsen's care with technical facts at NASA, as well as her accurate depiction of Johnson Space Center and the Houston area in general. Just a real fun read all-around, close to home for me, and nicely done!<br /><br />Gerritsen did a remarkable job blurring the line between modern-day science and science fiction. Gravity asks readers to consider the limits of secrecy that are justified in the name of "public safety." It also explores the limits of love and professional duty during times of crisis.<br /><br />I was delighted to recognize some professional acquaintances in the Acknowledgments, and I was saddened at the mention of Columbia (the novel pre-dated the tragedy). This was a touching read for me as our nation's Space Shuttle program, which is close to my heart, draws to its close. Heartily recommended for fans of medical thrillers or space aficionados. Required reading for JSC contractors and civil servants. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="17518385306535148710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2133327036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2133327036" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40231709-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600518090p2/40231709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2133327036?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/40231709-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007804955" href="/book/show/6390575-gravity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40231709-caitlin?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2133327036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5168725639942383224"><p><em>'Gravity'</em> is an action and science packed thriller with all the things you could want in a book- an awesome female main character who is both an astronaut and a doctor, intense scenes in space and in the NASA headquarters, and a creepy experiment gone wrong that is killing the crew members on the ISS one by one in a dark and disturbing way. This book was right up my alley. I thought everything about 'Gravity' was perfectly written and I am on the look out for my next Tess Gerristen novel.</p><br/><p>
  
   </p></span>
  <span id="freeText5168725639942383224" style="display:none"><p><em>'Gravity'</em> is an action and science packed thriller with all the things you could want in a book- an awesome female main character who is both an astronaut and a doctor, intense scenes in space and in the NASA headquarters, and a creepy experiment gone wrong that is killing the crew members on the ISS one by one in a dark and disturbing way. This book was right up my alley. I thought everything about 'Gravity' was perfectly written and I am on the look out for my next Tess Gerristen novel.</p><br /><p>
  
    <strong>What I Liked</strong>
  
</p><br /><p><strong>The Storyline-</strong>The plot of the book, how everything built with each major revelation about the deadly organism killing each astronaut and how everything fell apart piece by piece on the International Space Station in the middle of the void of space, was so interesting to read. While I had an idea of what was going to come next and where the story was heading, it was written in such a way that nothing was guaranteed and no one was safe.</p><br /><p><strong>The Science-</strong> I am a scientist at heart and a huge fan of medical thrillers and books with a dark undertone. The whole concept behind this whole book was very sound and just so thrilling to read, with just enough 'believable' science woven in to ground the story and make it just on the realm of possibility to make you feel unsettled. The extreme detail in NASA's operations, how the ISS works and the problems the astronauts and ground technicians face every launch, and of course the information about this deadly organism wrecking havoc both in space added so much depth to the story. I also have to comment on how gory the descriptions of the crew members deaths were, at times I internally grimaced at the imagery as it was quite vivid and added a whole new level to the intense story.</p><br /><p><strong>The Changing POV and Characters-</strong>I was going to discuss these two points separately but they tie in quite nicely together. Like most of the medical thrillers I have read, we get a change in POV throughout the book, switching between both minor and major characters to give us more insight into the story. Why this works particularly well in these types of books is that it firstly builds up suspense-especially when you either know that something is going to go wrong or you know a vital piece of information the main character is missing that would explain <em>everything</em>. Secondly, one of my favourite parts of these books is when the individual storylines come together and the plot pieces fall into place. I loved switching between Emma's and Jacks POV and seeing not only how each of the major events played out for both of them, but also how their relationship changes from each of their perspectives. Similarly, we meet minor characters throughout the book and it is always interesting how their small and often initially insignificant storylines contribute to the major plot arc.</p><br /><p>
  
    <strong>What I Didn't Like</strong>
  
</p><br /><p>I had no major problems with this book, it was such a fantastic read and I am really looking forward to reading more of her books.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="5168725639942383224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kelsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38665063-kelsey"><img alt="Kelsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581276552p2/38665063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2260290685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9260814774404068820">I've read a number of Gerritsen novels over the years; predominantly the Rizzoli + Isles series. Gravity was quite a jump from those, what with it being in space and all. At first I wasn't so sure how I'd connect with it as it's not my usual kind of setting for a read. HOWEVER, I thoroughly enjoyed it. The claustrophobia element of it had me feeling genuinely tense throughout, not to mention the detailed + downright disgusting (love it!!) descriptions of the symptoms, disease progression etc. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9260814774404068820" style="display:none">I've read a number of Gerritsen novels over the years; predominantly the Rizzoli + Isles series. Gravity was quite a jump from those, what with it being in space and all. At first I wasn't so sure how I'd connect with it as it's not my usual kind of setting for a read. HOWEVER, I thoroughly enjoyed it. The claustrophobia element of it had me feeling genuinely tense throughout, not to mention the detailed + downright disgusting (love it!!) descriptions of the symptoms, disease progression etc. The only slight issue was, whilst I admire the research, the use of a number of NASA terminology. There is a glossary at the back but I found myself not bothering going backwards + forwards to look up abbreviations. Still a definite 4 star read, without a doubt</span>
  <a data-text-id="9260814774404068820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333793744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7093896270680101825">Gravity, by tess Gerritsen, b-plus, Narrated by Campbell Scott, Produced by Simon and Schuster Audio, downloaded from audible.com<br/><br/>This is a stand-alone, a thriller. Dr. Emma Watson is a research scientist who has trained for much of a lifetime for what is now her dream, to be the chief physician assigned to a space voyage, to supervise the various research projects and to supervise the health of the other people on board. Her husband, Jack McCallum, an engineer, trained for space too but was forc</span>
  <span id="freeText7093896270680101825" style="display:none">Gravity, by tess Gerritsen, b-plus, Narrated by Campbell Scott, Produced by Simon and Schuster Audio, downloaded from audible.com<br /><br />This is a stand-alone, a thriller. Dr. Emma Watson is a research scientist who has trained for much of a lifetime for what is now her dream, to be the chief physician assigned to a space voyage, to supervise the various research projects and to supervise the health of the other people on board. Her husband, Jack McCallum, an engineer, trained for space too but was forced to give it up for health reasons, and this has left him embittered as he watches his wife train for a dream he shared with her. The lift-up goes fine, and things are fine until they reach the international space station. Then some of the mice start dying. They are told to jettison a particular experiment, which they do, but the cells included in this experiment go awry, people start dying, and the contagion continues to live and spill out of them contaminating the area. In the end, all the people are dead except for Emma, who has been exposed and is dying. By this time the army’s biohazards unit has taken over this space trip and now has told NASA that those remaining alive will not be allowed to come home because they might endanger people on earth-since they can’t determine what this lethal cell culture is, and what can be used to intervene and kill it. Jack, knowing he won’t be allowed to return to earth if he gets on the space station with Emma, wants to do it anyway so they can die together. McCallum is convinced that the army knows more about this terrible disease than it is telling NASA. So what is this dangerous organism? What causes it? And will they be able to find an intervention for it before Emma too is dead? And will they then be able to come home, or will they float in space forever. An entertaining thriller. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7093896270680101825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w1S2I0sJ2UGDdNIV+tJuHk47nD+3WBB3/QpGsjUt/JQwUiNcIr/C+La6KXDCMf91YG22PD1zTxAVxaBKhUkifg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NbdAm8WpVG5/FFVrUlG6e31F50BfuFi/0VUMyM1LZJjGsdXkrB9P10rarg5qsisQUxPNQ9WTB9g5muowfS+6cg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18149.Tess_Gerritsen">About Tess Gerritsen</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/18149.Tess_Gerritsen"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1416348007p3/18149.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/18149.Tess_Gerritsen">Tess Gerritsen
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12400532433060191135">Internationally bestselling author Tess Gerritsen took an unusual route to a writing career. A graduate of Stanford University, Tess went on to medical school at the University of California, San Francisco, where she was awarded her M.D.<br/><br/>While on maternity leave from her work as a physician, she began to write fiction. In 1987, her first novel was published. Call After Midnight, a romantic thriller</span>
  <span id="freeText12400532433060191135" style="display:none">Internationally bestselling author Tess Gerritsen took an unusual route to a writing career. A graduate of Stanford University, Tess went on to medical school at the University of California, San Francisco, where she was awarded her M.D.<br /><br />While on maternity leave from her work as a physician, she began to write fiction. In 1987, her first novel was published. Call After Midnight, a romantic thriller, was followed by eight more romantic suspense novels. She also wrote a screenplay, "Adrift", which aired as a 1993 CBS Movie of the Week starring Kate Jackson.<br /><br />Tess's first medical thriller, Harvest, was released in hardcover in 1996, and it marked her debut on the New York Times bestseller list. Her suspense novels since then have been: Life Support (1997), Bloodstream (1998), Gravity (1999), The Surgeon (2001), The Apprentice (2002), The Sinner (2003), Body Double (2004), Vanish (2005), The Mephisto Club (2006), and The Bone Garden (2007). Her books have been translated into 31 languages, and more than 15 million copies have been sold around the world.<br /><br />As well as being a New York Times bestselling author, she has also been a #1 bestseller in both Germany and the UK. She has won both the Nero Wolfe Award (for Vanish) and the Rita Award (for The Surgeon.) Critics around the world have praised her novels as "Pulse-pounding fun" (Philadelphia Inquirer), "Scary and brilliant" (Toronto Globe and Mail), and "Polished, riveting prose" (Chicago Tribune). Publisher Weekly has dubbed her the "medical suspense queen".<br /><br />Now retired from medicine, she writes full time. She lives in Maine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12400532433060191135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
